### How to use skills
- Discovery: The list above is the skills available in this session (name + description + file path). Skill bodies live on disk at the listed paths.
- Trigger rules: If the user names a skill (with $SkillName or plain text) OR the task clearly matches a skill's description shown above, you must use that skill for that turn. Multiple mentions mean use them all. Do not carry skills across turns unless re-mentioned.
- Missing/blocked: If a named skill isn't in the list or the path can't be read, say so briefly and continue with the best fallback.
- How to use a skill (progressive disclosure):
1) After deciding to use a skill, open its SKILL.md. Read only enough to follow the workflow.
2) When SKILL.md references relative paths (e.g., scripts/foo.py), resolve them relative to the skill directory listed above first, and only consider other paths if needed.
3) If SKILL.md points to extra folders such as references/, load only the specific files needed for the request; don't bulk-load everything.
4) If scripts/ exist, prefer running or patching them instead of retyping large code blocks.
5) If assets/ or templates exist, reuse them instead of recreating from scratch.
- Coordination and sequencing:
- If multiple skills apply, choose the minimal set that covers the request and state the order you'll use them.
- Announce which skill(s) you're using and why (one short line). If you skip an obvious skill, say why.
- Context hygiene:
- Keep context small: summarize long sections instead of pasting them; only load extra files when needed.
- Avoid deep reference-chasing: prefer opening only files directly linked from SKILL.md unless you're blocked.
- When variants exist (frameworks, providers, domains), pick only the relevant reference file(s) and note that choice.
- Safety and fallback: If a skill can't be applied cleanly (missing files, unclear instructions), state the issue, pick the next-best approach, and continue.

## Instruction Priority

Superpowers skills override default system prompt behavior, but **user instructions always take precedence**:

1. **User's explicit instructions** (CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, AGENTS.md, direct requests) 鈥?highest priority
2. **Superpowers skills** 鈥?override default system behavior where they conflict
3. **Default system prompt** 鈥?lowest priority

If CLAUDE.md, GEMINI.md, or AGENTS.md says "don't use TDD" and a skill says "always use TDD," follow the user's instructions. The user is in control.

## How to Access Skills

**In Claude Code:** Use the `Skill` tool. When you invoke a skill, its content is loaded and presented to you鈥攆ollow it directly. Never use the Read tool on skill files.

**In Gemini CLI:** Skills activate via the `activate_skill` tool. Gemini loads skill metadata at session start and activates the full content on demand.

**In other environments:** Check your platform's documentation for how skills are loaded.

## Platform Adaptation

Skills use Claude Code tool names. Non-CC platforms: see `references/codex-tools.md` (Codex) for tool equivalents. Gemini CLI users get the tool mapping loaded automatically via GEMINI.md.

# Using Skills

## The Rule

**Invoke relevant or requested skills BEFORE any response or action.** Even a 1% chance a skill might apply means that you should invoke the skill to check. If an invoked skill turns out to be wrong for the situation, you don't need to use it.

```dot
digraph skill_flow {
    "User message received" [shape=doublecircle];
    "About to EnterPlanMode?" [shape=doublecircle];
    "Already brainstormed?" [shape=diamond];
    "Invoke brainstorming skill" [shape=box];
    "Might any skill apply?" [shape=diamond];
    "Invoke Skill tool" [shape=box];
    "Announce: 'Using [skill] to [purpose]'" [shape=box];
    "Has checklist?" [shape=diamond];
    "Create TodoWrite todo per item" [shape=box];
    "Follow skill exactly" [shape=box];
    "Respond (including clarifications)" [shape=doublecircle];

    "About to EnterPlanMode?" -> "Already brainstormed?";
    "Already brainstormed?" -> "Invoke brainstorming skill" [label="no"];
    "Already brainstormed?" -> "Might any skill apply?" [label="yes"];
    "Invoke brainstorming skill" -> "Might any skill apply?";

    "User message received" -> "Might any skill apply?";
    "Might any skill apply?" -> "Invoke Skill tool" [label="yes, even 1%"];
    "Might any skill apply?" -> "Respond (including clarifications)" [label="definitely not"];
    "Invoke Skill tool" -> "Announce: 'Using [skill] to [purpose]'";
    "Announce: 'Using [skill] to [purpose]'" -> "Has checklist?";
    "Has checklist?" -> "Create TodoWrite todo per item" [label="yes"];
    "Has checklist?" -> "Follow skill exactly" [label="no"];
    "Create TodoWrite todo per item" -> "Follow skill exactly";
}
```

## Red Flags

These thoughts mean STOP鈥攜ou're rationalizing:

| Thought | Reality |
|---------|---------|
| "This is just a simple question" | Questions are tasks. Check for skills. |
| "I need more context first" | Skill check comes BEFORE clarifying questions. |
| "Let me explore the codebase first" | Skills tell you HOW to explore. Check first. |
| "I can check git/files quickly" | Files lack conversation context. Check for skills. |
| "Let me gather information first" | Skills tell you HOW to gather information. |
| "This doesn't need a formal skill" | If a skill exists, use it. |
| "I remember this skill" | Skills evolve. Read current version. |
| "This doesn't count as a task" | Action = task. Check for skills. |
| "The skill is overkill" | Simple things become complex. Use it. |
| "I'll just do this one thing first" | Check BEFORE doing anything. |
| "This feels productive" | Undisciplined action wastes time. Skills prevent this. |
| "I know what that means" | Knowing the concept 鈮?using the skill. Invoke it. |

## Skill Priority

When multiple skills could apply, use this order:

1. **Process skills first** (brainstorming, debugging) - these determine HOW to approach the task
2. **Implementation skills second** (frontend-design, mcp-builder) - these guide execution

"Let's build X" 鈫?brainstorming first, then implementation skills.
"Fix this bug" 鈫?debugging first, then domain-specific skills.

## Skill Types

**Rigid** (TDD, debugging): Follow exactly. Don't adapt away discipline.

**Flexible** (patterns): Adapt principles to context.

The skill itself tells you which.

## User Instructions

Instructions say WHAT, not HOW. "Add X" or "Fix Y" doesn't mean skip workflows.

# Brainstorming Ideas Into Designs

Help turn ideas into fully formed designs and specs through natural collaborative dialogue.

Start by understanding the current project context, then ask questions one at a time to refine the idea. Once you understand what you're building, present the design and get user approval.

<HARD-GATE>
Do NOT invoke any implementation skill, write any code, scaffold any project, or take any implementation action until you have presented a design and the user has approved it. This applies to EVERY project regardless of perceived simplicity.
</HARD-GATE>

## Anti-Pattern: "This Is Too Simple To Need A Design"

Every project goes through this process. A todo list, a single-function utility, a config change 鈥?all of them. "Simple" projects are where unexamined assumptions cause the most wasted work. The design can be short (a few sentences for truly simple projects), but you MUST present it and get approval.

## Checklist

You MUST create a task for each of these items and complete them in order:

1. **Explore project context** 鈥?check files, docs, recent commits
2. **Offer visual companion** (if topic will involve visual questions) 鈥?this is its own message, not combined with a clarifying question. See the Visual Companion section below.
3. **Ask clarifying questions** 鈥?one at a time, understand purpose/constraints/success criteria
4. **Propose 2-3 approaches** 鈥?with trade-offs and your recommendation
5. **Present design** 鈥?in sections scaled to their complexity, get user approval after each section
6. **Write design doc** 鈥?save to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md` and commit
7. **Spec self-review** 鈥?quick inline check for placeholders, contradictions, ambiguity, scope (see below)
8. **User reviews written spec** 鈥?ask user to review the spec file before proceeding
9. **Transition to implementation** 鈥?invoke writing-plans skill to create implementation plan

## Process Flow

```dot
digraph brainstorming {
    "Explore project context" [shape=box];
    "Visual questions ahead?" [shape=diamond];
    "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" [shape=box];
    "Ask clarifying questions" [shape=box];
    "Propose 2-3 approaches" [shape=box];
    "Present design sections" [shape=box];
    "User approves design?" [shape=diamond];
    "Write design doc" [shape=box];
    "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" [shape=box];
    "User reviews spec?" [shape=diamond];
    "Invoke writing-plans skill" [shape=doublecircle];

    "Explore project context" -> "Visual questions ahead?";
    "Visual questions ahead?" -> "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" [label="yes"];
    "Visual questions ahead?" -> "Ask clarifying questions" [label="no"];
    "Offer Visual Companion\n(own message, no other content)" -> "Ask clarifying questions";
    "Ask clarifying questions" -> "Propose 2-3 approaches";
    "Propose 2-3 approaches" -> "Present design sections";
    "Present design sections" -> "User approves design?";
    "User approves design?" -> "Present design sections" [label="no, revise"];
    "User approves design?" -> "Write design doc" [label="yes"];
    "Write design doc" -> "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)";
    "Spec self-review\n(fix inline)" -> "User reviews spec?";
    "User reviews spec?" -> "Write design doc" [label="changes requested"];
    "User reviews spec?" -> "Invoke writing-plans skill" [label="approved"];
}
```

**The terminal state is invoking writing-plans.** Do NOT invoke frontend-design, mcp-builder, or any other implementation skill. The ONLY skill you invoke after brainstorming is writing-plans.

## The Process

**Understanding the idea:**

- Check out the current project state first (files, docs, recent commits)
- Before asking detailed questions, assess scope: if the request describes multiple independent subsystems (e.g., "build a platform with chat, file storage, billing, and analytics"), flag this immediately. Don't spend questions refining details of a project that needs to be decomposed first.
- If the project is too large for a single spec, help the user decompose into sub-projects: what are the independent pieces, how do they relate, what order should they be built? Then brainstorm the first sub-project through the normal design flow. Each sub-project gets its own spec 鈫?plan 鈫?implementation cycle.
- For appropriately-scoped projects, ask questions one at a time to refine the idea
- Prefer multiple choice questions when possible, but open-ended is fine too
- Only one question per message - if a topic needs more exploration, break it into multiple questions
- Focus on understanding: purpose, constraints, success criteria

**Exploring approaches:**

- Propose 2-3 different approaches with trade-offs
- Present options conversationally with your recommendation and reasoning
- Lead with your recommended option and explain why

**Presenting the design:**

- Once you believe you understand what you're building, present the design
- Scale each section to its complexity: a few sentences if straightforward, up to 200-300 words if nuanced
- Ask after each section whether it looks right so far
- Cover: architecture, components, data flow, error handling, testing
- Be ready to go back and clarify if something doesn't make sense

**Design for isolation and clarity:**

- Break the system into smaller units that each have one clear purpose, communicate through well-defined interfaces, and can be understood and tested independently
- For each unit, you should be able to answer: what does it do, how do you use it, and what does it depend on?
- Can someone understand what a unit does without reading its internals? Can you change the internals without breaking consumers? If not, the boundaries need work.
- Smaller, well-bounded units are also easier for you to work with - you reason better about code you can hold in context at once, and your edits are more reliable when files are focused. When a file grows large, that's often a signal that it's doing too much.

**Working in existing codebases:**

- Explore the current structure before proposing changes. Follow existing patterns.
- Where existing code has problems that affect the work (e.g., a file that's grown too large, unclear boundaries, tangled responsibilities), include targeted improvements as part of the design - the way a good developer improves code they're working in.
- Don't propose unrelated refactoring. Stay focused on what serves the current goal.

## After the Design

**Documentation:**

- Write the validated design (spec) to `docs/superpowers/specs/YYYY-MM-DD-<topic>-design.md`
  - (User preferences for spec location override this default)
- Use elements-of-style:writing-clearly-and-concisely skill if available
- Commit the design document to git

**Spec Self-Review:**
After writing the spec document, look at it with fresh eyes:

1. **Placeholder scan:** Any "TBD", "TODO", incomplete sections, or vague requirements? Fix them.
2. **Internal consistency:** Do any sections contradict each other? Does the architecture match the feature descriptions?
3. **Scope check:** Is this focused enough for a single implementation plan, or does it need decomposition?
4. **Ambiguity check:** Could any requirement be interpreted two different ways? If so, pick one and make it explicit.

Fix any issues inline. No need to re-review 鈥?just fix and move on.

**User Review Gate:**
After the spec review loop passes, ask the user to review the written spec before proceeding:

> "Spec written and committed to `<path>`. Please review it and let me know if you want to make any changes before we start writing out the implementation plan."

Wait for the user's response. If they request changes, make them and re-run the spec review loop. Only proceed once the user approves.

**Implementation:**

- Invoke the writing-plans skill to create a detailed implementation plan
- Do NOT invoke any other skill. writing-plans is the next step.

## Key Principles

- **One question at a time** - Don't overwhelm with multiple questions
- **Multiple choice preferred** - Easier to answer than open-ended when possible
- **YAGNI ruthlessly** - Remove unnecessary features from all designs
- **Explore alternatives** - Always propose 2-3 approaches before settling
- **Incremental validation** - Present design, get approval before moving on
- **Be flexible** - Go back and clarify when something doesn't make sense

## Visual Companion

A browser-based companion for showing mockups, diagrams, and visual options during brainstorming. Available as a tool 鈥?not a mode. Accepting the companion means it's available for questions that benefit from visual treatment; it does NOT mean every question goes through the browser.

**Offering the companion:** When you anticipate that upcoming questions will involve visual content (mockups, layouts, diagrams), offer it once for consent:
> "Some of what we're working on might be easier to explain if I can show it to you in a web browser. I can put together mockups, diagrams, comparisons, and other visuals as we go. This feature is still new and can be token-intensive. Want to try it? (Requires opening a local URL)"

**This offer MUST be its own message.** Do not combine it with clarifying questions, context summaries, or any other content. The message should contain ONLY the offer above and nothing else. Wait for the user's response before continuing. If they decline, proceed with text-only brainstorming.

**Per-question decision:** Even after the user accepts, decide FOR EACH QUESTION whether to use the browser or the terminal. The test: **would the user understand this better by seeing it than reading it?**

- **Use the browser** for content that IS visual 鈥?mockups, wireframes, layout comparisons, architecture diagrams, side-by-side visual designs
- **Use the terminal** for content that is text 鈥?requirements questions, conceptual choices, tradeoff lists, A/B/C/D text options, scope decisions

A question about a UI topic is not automatically a visual question. "What does personality mean in this context?" is a conceptual question 鈥?use the terminal. "Which wizard layout works better?" is a visual question 鈥?use the browser.

If they agree to the companion, read the detailed guide before proceeding:
`skills/brainstorming/visual-companion.md`

# Test-Driven Development (TDD)

## Overview

Write the test first. Watch it fail. Write minimal code to pass.

**Core principle:** If you didn't watch the test fail, you don't know if it tests the right thing.

**Violating the letter of the rules is violating the spirit of the rules.**

## When to Use

**Always:**
- New features
- Bug fixes
- Refactoring
- Behavior changes

**Exceptions (ask your human partner):**
- Throwaway prototypes
- Generated code
- Configuration files

Thinking "skip TDD just this once"? Stop. That's rationalization.

## The Iron Law

```
NO PRODUCTION CODE WITHOUT A FAILING TEST FIRST
```

Write code before the test? Delete it. Start over.

**No exceptions:**
- Don't keep it as "reference"
- Don't "adapt" it while writing tests
- Don't look at it
- Delete means delete

Implement fresh from tests. Period.

## Red-Green-Refactor

```dot
digraph tdd_cycle {
    rankdir=LR;
    red [label="RED\nWrite failing test", shape=box, style=filled, fillcolor="#ffcccc"];
    verify_red [label="Verify fails\ncorrectly", shape=diamond];
    green [label="GREEN\nMinimal code", shape=box, style=filled, fillcolor="#ccffcc"];
    verify_green [label="Verify passes\nAll green", shape=diamond];
    refactor [label="REFACTOR\nClean up", shape=box, style=filled, fillcolor="#ccccff"];
    next [label="Next", shape=ellipse];

    red -> verify_red;
    verify_red -> green [label="yes"];
    verify_red -> red [label="wrong\nfailure"];
    green -> verify_green;
    verify_green -> refactor [label="yes"];
    verify_green -> green [label="no"];
    refactor -> verify_green [label="stay\ngreen"];
    verify_green -> next;
    next -> red;
}
```

### RED - Write Failing Test

Write one minimal test showing what should happen.

<Good>
```typescript
test('retries failed operations 3 times', async () => {
  let attempts = 0;
  const operation = () => {
    attempts++;
    if (attempts < 3) throw new Error('fail');
    return 'success';
  };

  const result = await retryOperation(operation);

  expect(result).toBe('success');
  expect(attempts).toBe(3);
});
```
Clear name, tests real behavior, one thing
</Good>

<Bad>
```typescript
test('retry works', async () => {
  const mock = jest.fn()
    .mockRejectedValueOnce(new Error())
    .mockRejectedValueOnce(new Error())
    .mockResolvedValueOnce('success');
  await retryOperation(mock);
  expect(mock).toHaveBeenCalledTimes(3);
});
```
Vague name, tests mock not code
</Bad>

**Requirements:**
- One behavior
- Clear name
- Real code (no mocks unless unavoidable)

### Verify RED - Watch It Fail

**MANDATORY. Never skip.**

```bash
npm test path/to/test.test.ts
```

Confirm:
- Test fails (not errors)
- Failure message is expected
- Fails because feature missing (not typos)

**Test passes?** You're testing existing behavior. Fix test.

**Test errors?** Fix error, re-run until it fails correctly.

### GREEN - Minimal Code

Write simplest code to pass the test.

<Good>
```typescript
async function retryOperation<T>(fn: () => Promise<T>): Promise<T> {
  for (let i = 0; i < 3; i++) {
    try {
      return await fn();
    } catch (e) {
      if (i === 2) throw e;
    }
  }
  throw new Error('unreachable');
}
```
Just enough to pass
</Good>

<Bad>
```typescript
async function retryOperation<T>(
  fn: () => Promise<T>,
  options?: {
    maxRetries?: number;
    backoff?: 'linear' | 'exponential';
    onRetry?: (attempt: number) => void;
  }
): Promise<T> {
  // YAGNI
}
```
Over-engineered
</Bad>

Don't add features, refactor other code, or "improve" beyond the test.

### Verify GREEN - Watch It Pass

**MANDATORY.**

```bash
npm test path/to/test.test.ts
```

Confirm:
- Test passes
- Other tests still pass
- Output pristine (no errors, warnings)

**Test fails?** Fix code, not test.

**Other tests fail?** Fix now.

### REFACTOR - Clean Up

After green only:
- Remove duplication
- Improve names
- Extract helpers

Keep tests green. Don't add behavior.

### Repeat

Next failing test for next feature.

## Good Tests

| Quality | Good | Bad |
|---------|------|-----|
| **Minimal** | One thing. "and" in name? Split it. | `test('validates email and domain and whitespace')` |
| **Clear** | Name describes behavior | `test('test1')` |
| **Shows intent** | Demonstrates desired API | Obscures what code should do |

## Why Order Matters

**"I'll write tests after to verify it works"**

Tests written after code pass immediately. Passing immediately proves nothing:
- Might test wrong thing
- Might test implementation, not behavior
- Might miss edge cases you forgot
- You never saw it catch the bug

Test-first forces you to see the test fail, proving it actually tests something.

**"I already manually tested all the edge cases"**

Manual testing is ad-hoc. You think you tested everything but:
- No record of what you tested
- Can't re-run when code changes
- Easy to forget cases under pressure
- "It worked when I tried it" 鈮?comprehensive

Automated tests are systematic. They run the same way every time.

**"Deleting X hours of work is wasteful"**

Sunk cost fallacy. The time is already gone. Your choice now:
- Delete and rewrite with TDD (X more hours, high confidence)
- Keep it and add tests after (30 min, low confidence, likely bugs)

The "waste" is keeping code you can't trust. Working code without real tests is technical debt.

**"TDD is dogmatic, being pragmatic means adapting"**

TDD IS pragmatic:
- Finds bugs before commit (faster than debugging after)
- Prevents regressions (tests catch breaks immediately)
- Documents behavior (tests show how to use code)
- Enables refactoring (change freely, tests catch breaks)

"Pragmatic" shortcuts = debugging in production = slower.

**"Tests after achieve the same goals - it's spirit not ritual"**

No. Tests-after answer "What does this do?" Tests-first answer "What should this do?"

Tests-after are biased by your implementation. You test what you built, not what's required. You verify remembered edge cases, not discovered ones.

Tests-first force edge case discovery before implementing. Tests-after verify you remembered everything (you didn't).

30 minutes of tests after 鈮?TDD. You get coverage, lose proof tests work.

## Common Rationalizations

| Excuse | Reality |
|--------|---------|
| "Too simple to test" | Simple code breaks. Test takes 30 seconds. |
| "I'll test after" | Tests passing immediately prove nothing. |
| "Tests after achieve same goals" | Tests-after = "what does this do?" Tests-first = "what should this do?" |
| "Already manually tested" | Ad-hoc 鈮?systematic. No record, can't re-run. |
| "Deleting X hours is wasteful" | Sunk cost fallacy. Keeping unverified code is technical debt. |
| "Keep as reference, write tests first" | You'll adapt it. That's testing after. Delete means delete. |
| "Need to explore first" | Fine. Throw away exploration, start with TDD. |
| "Test hard = design unclear" | Listen to test. Hard to test = hard to use. |
| "TDD will slow me down" | TDD faster than debugging. Pragmatic = test-first. |
| "Manual test faster" | Manual doesn't prove edge cases. You'll re-test every change. |
| "Existing code has no tests" | You're improving it. Add tests for existing code. |

## Red Flags - STOP and Start Over

- Code before test
- Test after implementation
- Test passes immediately
- Can't explain why test failed
- Tests added "later"
- Rationalizing "just this once"
- "I already manually tested it"
- "Tests after achieve the same purpose"
- "It's about spirit not ritual"
- "Keep as reference" or "adapt existing code"
- "Already spent X hours, deleting is wasteful"
- "TDD is dogmatic, I'm being pragmatic"
- "This is different because..."

**All of these mean: Delete code. Start over with TDD.**

## Example: Bug Fix

**Bug:** Empty email accepted

**RED**
```typescript
test('rejects empty email', async () => {
  const result = await submitForm({ email: '' });
  expect(result.error).toBe('Email required');
});
```

**Verify RED**
```bash
$ npm test
FAIL: expected 'Email required', got undefined
```

**GREEN**
```typescript
function submitForm(data: FormData) {
  if (!data.email?.trim()) {
    return { error: 'Email required' };
  }
  // ...
}
```

**Verify GREEN**
```bash
$ npm test
PASS
```

**REFACTOR**
Extract validation for multiple fields if needed.

## Verification Checklist

Before marking work complete:

- [ ] Every new function/method has a test
- [ ] Watched each test fail before implementing
- [ ] Each test failed for expected reason (feature missing, not typo)
- [ ] Wrote minimal code to pass each test
- [ ] All tests pass
- [ ] Output pristine (no errors, warnings)
- [ ] Tests use real code (mocks only if unavoidable)
- [ ] Edge cases and errors covered

Can't check all boxes? You skipped TDD. Start over.

## When Stuck

| Problem | Solution |
|---------|----------|
| Don't know how to test | Write wished-for API. Write assertion first. Ask your human partner. |
| Test too complicated | Design too complicated. Simplify interface. |
| Must mock everything | Code too coupled. Use dependency injection. |
| Test setup huge | Extract helpers. Still complex? Simplify design. |

## Debugging Integration

Bug found? Write failing test reproducing it. Follow TDD cycle. Test proves fix and prevents regression.

Never fix bugs without a test.

## Testing Anti-Patterns

When adding mocks or test utilities, read @testing-anti-patterns.md to avoid common pitfalls:
- Testing mock behavior instead of real behavior
- Adding test-only methods to production classes
- Mocking without understanding dependencies

## Final Rule

```
Production code 鈫?test exists and failed first
Otherwise 鈫?not TDD
```

No exceptions without your human partner's permission.

            redis_client=self.redis_client,
            namespace=str(getattr(config, "redis_namespace", "clonecut_worker:")),
            logger=self.logger,
        )
        self.dedup_ttl_seconds = max(60, int(self._get_queue_cfg("dedup_ttl_seconds", 24 * 3600)))
        self.queue_adapter = RedisQueueAdapter(
            redis_client=self.redis_client,
            namespace=str(getattr(config, "redis_namespace", "clonecut_worker:")),
            dedup_ttl_seconds=self.dedup_ttl_seconds,
            logger=self.logger,
        )
        self.use_redis_queue = self.queue_adapter.is_persistent()
        self.task_storage = self._init_task_storage()
        self.lock = RLock()
        self.stop_event = Event()
        self.worker_threads: List[Thread] = []
        self.active_workers: Dict[str, int] = {
            "download": 0,
            "process": 0,
            "upload": 0,
        }

        self.stats: Dict[str, int] = {
            "received": 0,
            "completed": 0,
            "failed": 0,
            "running": 0,
            "retried": 0,
            "zombie_reclaimed": 0,
        }

        self.max_download_workers = max(1, int(self._get_worker_cfg("max_download_workers", 2)))
        self.max_process_workers = max(1, int(self._get_worker_cfg("max_process_workers", 2)))
        self.max_upload_workers = max(1, int(self._get_worker_cfg("max_upload_workers", 2)))
        self.download_timeout_seconds = max(
            30,
            int(self._get_worker_cfg("download_timeout_seconds", 600)),
        )
        self.download_chunk_size = max(
            1024,
            int(self._get_worker_cfg("download_chunk_size", 8192)),
        )
        self.max_retries_default = max(0, int(self._get_queue_cfg("max_retries", 3)))
        self.retry_backoff_seconds = self._parse_retry_backoff(
            self._get_queue_cfg("retry_backoff_seconds", [5, 10, 20])
        )
        self.upload_retry_backoff_seconds = self._parse_retry_backoff(
            self._get_worker_cfg("upload_retry_backoff_seconds", [1, 2, 4])
        )
        self.retry_check_interval_seconds = max(
            0.2,
            float(self._get_worker_cfg("retry_check_interval_seconds", 1.0)),
        )
        self.zombie_timeout_seconds = max(
            self.download_timeout_seconds,
            int(self._get_worker_cfg("zombie_timeout_seconds", 7200)),
        )
        self.zombie_check_interval_seconds = max(
            2.0,
            float(self._get_worker_cfg("zombie_check_interval_seconds", 300.0)),
        )
        self.zombie_timeout_by_status_seconds = self._build_zombie_timeout_by_status()
        self.retry_heap: List[Tuple[float, str]] = []
        self.retry_index: Dict[str, Tuple[float, UnifiedTask]] = {}
        self.active_task_ids: set[str] = set()

        Path(self.config.input_dir).mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        Path(self.config.output_dir).mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        self.upload_root = Path(self.config.output_dir) / "_uploaded"
        self.upload_root.mkdir(parents=True, exist_ok=True)
        self.upload_storage_backend = str(
            self._get_worker_cfg("upload_storage_backend", "local")
        ).strip().lower() or "local"
        if self.upload_storage_backend != "local":
            self.logger.warning(
                "unsupported upload storage backend=%s, fallback to local",
                self.upload_storage_backend,
            )
            self.upload_storage_backend = "local"
        self.storage_adapter: UploadStorageAdapter = build_default_storage_adapter(
            upload_root=str(self.upload_root),
            logger=self.logger,
        )
        self.forum_upload_enabled = self._bool_cfg(
            os.getenv("CLONECUT_FORUM_UPLOAD_ENABLED"),
            bool(self._get_worker_cfg("forum_upload_enabled", True)),
        )
        self.forum_reply_content = str(
            self._get_worker_cfg("forum_reply_content", "Video processing completed")
        ).strip() or "Video processing completed"
        self.forum_settings_path = str(
            self._get_worker_cfg("forum_settings_path", "config/forum_settings.yaml")
        ).strip() or "config/forum_settings.yaml"

        self.tts_adapter_enabled = self._bool_cfg(
            os.getenv("CLONECUT_TTS_ENABLE"),
            bool(self._get_worker_cfg("tts_enable", True)),
        )
        tts_engine_mode_raw = str(
            os.getenv("CLONECUT_TTS_ENGINE", self._get_worker_cfg("tts_engine", "local"))
        ).strip().lower()
        if tts_engine_mode_raw not in {"local", "http", "auto"}:
            tts_engine_mode_raw = "local"
        self.tts_engine_mode = tts_engine_mode_raw
        tts_default_voice = str(self._get_worker_cfg("tts_default_voice", ""))
        tts_api_endpoint = str(self._get_worker_cfg("tts_api_endpoint", ""))
        tts_api_timeout_raw = self._get_worker_cfg("tts_api_timeout_seconds", 15)
        tts_local_sample_rate_raw = self._get_worker_cfg("tts_local_sample_rate_hz", 24000)
        try:
            tts_api_timeout = float(tts_api_timeout_raw)
        except Exception:
            tts_api_timeout = 15.0
        try:
            tts_local_sample_rate = int(tts_local_sample_rate_raw)
        except Exception:
            tts_local_sample_rate = 24000
        tts_local_sample_rate_env = os.getenv(
            "CLONECUT_TTS_LOCAL_SAMPLE_RATE_HZ",
            str(tts_local_sample_rate),
        )
        try:
            tts_local_sample_rate_value = int(tts_local_sample_rate_env)
        except Exception:
            tts_local_sample_rate_value = tts_local_sample_rate
        self.tts_local_adapter = LocalTtsAdapter(
            enabled=self.tts_adapter_enabled,
            output_dir=self.config.output_dir,
            default_voice=os.getenv("CLONECUT_TTS_DEFAULT_VOICE", tts_default_voice),
            sample_rate_hz=tts_local_sample_rate_value,
            logger=self.logger,
        )
        self.tts_http_adapter = HttpTtsAdapter(
            enabled=self.tts_adapter_enabled,
            default_voice=os.getenv("CLONECUT_TTS_DEFAULT_VOICE", tts_default_voice),
            api_endpoint=os.getenv("CLONECUT_TTS_API_ENDPOINT", tts_api_endpoint),
            api_timeout_seconds=float(
                os.getenv("CLONECUT_TTS_API_TIMEOUT_SECONDS", str(tts_api_timeout))
            ),
            logger=self.logger,
        )

        video_cmd = str(self._get_worker_cfg("video_command_template", ""))
        video_timeout_raw = self._get_worker_cfg("video_command_timeout_seconds", 7200)
        try:
            video_timeout = int(video_timeout_raw)
        except Exception:
            video_timeout = 7200
        self.video_adapter = ExternalVideoCommandAdapter(
            output_dir=self.config.output_dir,
            command_template=os.getenv("CLONECUT_VIDEO_COMMAND_TEMPLATE", video_cmd),
            timeout_seconds=int(
                os.getenv("CLONECUT_VIDEO_COMMAND_TIMEOUT_SECONDS", str(video_timeout))
            ),
            logger=self.logger,
        )
        self.internal_pipeline_enabled = self._bool_cfg(
            os.getenv("CLONECUT_USE_INTERNAL_PIPELINE"),
            bool(self._get_worker_cfg("use_internal_pipeline", False)),
        )
        runner_mode_raw = str(
            os.getenv(
                "CLONECUT_INTERNAL_PIPELINE_RUNNER",
                self._get_worker_cfg("internal_pipeline_runner", "subprocess"),
            )
            or ""
        ).strip().lower()
        if runner_mode_raw not in {"subprocess", "warm_process"}:
            runner_mode_raw = "subprocess"
        self.internal_pipeline_runner_mode = runner_mode_raw
        self.internal_pipeline_pool_size = max(
            1,
            int(self._get_worker_cfg("internal_pipeline_pool_size", 1)),
        )
        self.internal_pipeline_warmup_on_start = self._bool_cfg(
            os.getenv("CLONECUT_INTERNAL_PIPELINE_WARMUP"),
            bool(self._get_worker_cfg("internal_pipeline_warmup_on_start", True)),
        )
        self.internal_pipeline_runner: Optional[InternalPipelineWarmRunner] = None
        if self.internal_pipeline_runner_mode == "warm_process":
            repo_root = Path(__file__).resolve().parents[2]
            self.internal_pipeline_runner = InternalPipelineWarmRunner(
                repo_root=str(repo_root),
                output_dir=str(self.config.output_dir),
                pool_size=self.internal_pipeline_pool_size,
                warmup_on_start=self.internal_pipeline_warmup_on_start,
                base_env=self._build_internal_pipeline_env(),
                logger=self.logger,
            )

        # --- telemetry ---
        telemetry_interval = float(self._get_worker_cfg("resource_monitor_interval_seconds", 5.0))
        report_dir = str(self._get_worker_cfg("performance_report_dir", "logs/performance_reports"))
        self.resource_monitor = ResourceMonitor(
            interval_seconds=telemetry_interval,
            disk_path=str(self.config.output_dir),
            logger=self.logger,
        )
        self.performance_tracker = PerformanceTracker(resource_monitor=self.resource_monitor)
        self.report_generator = ReportGenerator(report_dir=report_dir, logger=self.logger)

    def start(self) -> None:
        if any(thread.is_alive() for thread in self.worker_threads):
            return

        if self.internal_pipeline_runner is not None:
            self.internal_pipeline_runner.start()
        self.resource_monitor.start()
        recovered = self._recover_stuck_tasks()
        restored_retries = self._restore_retry_schedule()
        self.stop_event.clear()
        self.worker_threads = []
        self._spawn_workers("download", self.max_download_workers, self._download_loop)
        self._spawn_workers("process", self.max_process_workers, self._process_loop)
        self._spawn_workers("upload", self.max_upload_workers, self._upload_loop)
        self._spawn_workers("retry", 1, self._retry_scheduler_loop)
        self._spawn_workers("zombie", 1, self._zombie_cleaner_loop)

        self.logger.info(
            "worker adapters: tts_enabled=%s tts_engine=%s tts_http_ready=%s video_cmd_enabled=%s internal_pipeline=%s redis_registry=%s redis_queue=%s recovered=%s restored_retries=%s",
            self.tts_adapter_enabled,
            self.tts_engine_mode,
            self.tts_http_adapter.is_ready(),
            self.video_adapter.is_enabled(),
            self.internal_pipeline_enabled,
            self.registry.is_persistent(),
            self.use_redis_queue,
            recovered,
            restored_retries,
        )
        self.logger.info(
            "worker pools started: download=%s process=%s upload=%s retry_scheduler=%s zombie_timeout=%ss zombie_by_status=%s internal_runner=%s warm_pool=%s",
            self.max_download_workers,
            self.max_process_workers,
            self.max_upload_workers,
            1,
            self.zombie_timeout_seconds,
            self.zombie_timeout_by_status_seconds,
            self.internal_pipeline_runner_mode,
            self.internal_pipeline_pool_size if self.internal_pipeline_runner is not None else 0,
        )

    def stop(self) -> None:
        self.stop_event.set()
        for thread in self.worker_threads:
            thread.join(timeout=2.0)
        if self.internal_pipeline_runner is not None:
            self.internal_pipeline_runner.stop()
        self.resource_monitor.stop()
        self.logger.info("worker service stopped")

    def submit(self, raw_data: Dict[str, Any]) -> Tuple[bool, str, Optional[str]]:
        try:
            task = self._build_task(raw_data)
        except ValueError as exc:
            return False, "", str(exc)

        existing_task_id = self.queue_adapter.check_duplicate(task)
        if existing_task_id:
            self.logger.info(
                "duplicate task ignored: incoming=%s existing=%s",
                task.task_id,
                existing_task_id,
            )
            return True, existing_task_id, None

        self._persist_task(task)
        self.queue_adapter.remember_dedup(task, ttl_seconds=self.dedup_ttl_seconds)
        self._enqueue_task(self._initial_queue_for_task(task), task)

        with self.lock:
            self.stats["received"] += 1

        self.logger.info(
            "task received: task_id=%s type=%s queued=%s",
            task.task_id,
            task.task_type.value,
            self._initial_queue_for_task(task),
        )
        return True, task.task_id, None

    def get_status(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        queue_sizes = self.queue_adapter.get_queue_sizes()
        queued_total = (
            int(queue_sizes.get("download", 0))
            + int(queue_sizes.get("process", 0))
            + int(queue_sizes.get("upload", 0))
        )
        task_status_counts = self.get_task_status_counts()

        with self.lock:
            running = sum(self.active_workers.values())
            stats = dict(self.stats)
            active_workers = dict(self.active_workers)
        active_task_count = (
            int(task_status_counts.get(TaskStatus.PENDING.value, 0))
            + int(task_status_counts.get(TaskStatus.ASSIGNED.value, 0))
            + int(task_status_counts.get(TaskStatus.DOWNLOADING.value, 0))
            + int(task_status_counts.get(TaskStatus.PROCESSING.value, 0))
            + int(task_status_counts.get(TaskStatus.UPLOADING.value, 0))
        )
        status_metrics = {
            "total": int(task_status_counts.get("total", 0)),
            "completed": int(task_status_counts.get(TaskStatus.COMPLETED.value, 0)),
            "failed": int(task_status_counts.get(TaskStatus.FAILED.value, 0)),
            "active": int(active_task_count),
            "zombie": int(stats["zombie_reclaimed"]),
            "retried": int(stats["retried"]),
            "received": int(stats["received"]),
        }

        return {
            "status": "online",
            "is_busy": running > 0 or queued_total > 0,
            "total_queue_size": queued_total + running,
            "queue_sizes": queue_sizes,
            "queues": {
                "download": int(queue_sizes.get("download", 0)),
                "process": int(queue_sizes.get("process", 0)),
                "upload": int(queue_sizes.get("upload", 0)),
                "pending": queued_total,
                "processing": active_workers.get("process", 0),
                "completed": stats["completed"],
                "failed": stats["failed"],
                "retried": stats["retried"],
                "received": stats["received"],
                "active": active_task_count,
                "total": int(task_status_counts.get("total", 0)),
                "zombie_reclaimed": stats["zombie_reclaimed"],
                "zombie": stats["zombie_reclaimed"],
            },
            "workers": active_workers,
            "status_metrics": status_metrics,
            "task_status_counts": task_status_counts,
            "uptime_seconds": int(max(0, time.time() - self.booted_at)),
            "timestamp": time.time(),
        }

    def get_resources(self) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        return self.resource_monitor.get_current()

    def get_resources_history(self, minutes: int = 60) -> list:
        return self.resource_monitor.get_history(minutes=minutes)

    def get_task(self, task_id: str) -> Optional[Dict[str, Any]]:
        task = self.registry.get(task_id)
        if task is None:
            return None
        return task.to_dict()

    def get_task_status_counts(self) -> Dict[str, int]:
        counts: Dict[str, int] = {}
        for status in self._queryable_statuses():
            counts[status.value] = int(self.registry.count_by_status(status))
        counts["total"] = sum(counts.values())
        return counts

    def list_tasks(
        self,
        status: Optional[str] = None,
        limit: int = 20,
        offset: int = 0,
    ) -> Dict[str, Any]:
        size = max(1, min(200, int(limit)))
        start = max(0, int(offset))
        target_statuses = self._resolve_status_filter(status)
        read_limit = min(5000, start + size)

        if len(target_statuses) == 1:
            selected = target_statuses[0]
            total = int(self.registry.count_by_status(selected))
            tasks = self.registry.list_by_status(selected, limit=max(1, read_limit))
        else:
            total = 0
            merged: Dict[str, UnifiedTask] = {}
            for st in target_statuses:
                total += int(self.registry.count_by_status(st))
                for task in self.registry.list_by_status(st, limit=max(1, read_limit)):
                    merged[task.task_id] = task
            tasks = list(merged.values())
            tasks.sort(key=lambda item: item.created_at, reverse=True)

        selected_tasks = tasks[start : start + size]
        return {
            "total": total,
            "limit": size,
            "offset": start,
            "tasks": [item.to_dict() for item in selected_tasks],
        }

    def cancel_task(self, task_id: str) -> Tuple[bool, str]:
        task = self.registry.get(task_id)
        if task is None:
            return False, "task not…19680 tokens truncated…    )
        cover_middle = self._pick_first_text(
            merged.get("cover_title_middle"),
            merged.get("灏侀潰鏍囬涓?),
            payload.get("cover_title_middle"),
            payload.get("灏侀潰鏍囬涓?),
            metadata.get("cover_title_middle"),
            metadata.get("灏侀潰鏍囬涓?),
        )
        cover_down = self._pick_first_text(
            merged.get("cover_title_down"),
            merged.get("灏侀潰鏍囬涓?),
            payload.get("cover_title_down"),
            payload.get("灏侀潰鏍囬涓?),
            metadata.get("cover_title_down"),
            metadata.get("灏侀潰鏍囬涓?),
        )

        cover_titles = self._normalize_text_list(merged.get("cover_titles"))
        if not cover_up and len(cover_titles) >= 1:
            cover_up = cover_titles[0]
        if not cover_middle and len(cover_titles) >= 2:
            cover_middle = cover_titles[1]
        if not cover_down and len(cover_titles) >= 3:
            cover_down = cover_titles[2]

        compact_titles = [text for text in (cover_up, cover_middle, cover_down) if text]
        if compact_titles:
            merged["cover_titles"] = compact_titles
            merged["cover_title_up"] = cover_up
            merged["cover_title_middle"] = cover_middle
            merged["cover_title_down"] = cover_down
            merged["灏侀潰鏍囬涓?] = cover_up
            merged["灏侀潰鏍囬涓?] = cover_middle
            merged["灏侀潰鏍囬涓?] = cover_down

        speaker = self._pick_first_text(
            merged.get("speaker"),
            merged.get("speaker_id"),
            merged.get("spk"),
            merged.get("target_speaker"),
        )
        if speaker:
            merged["speaker"] = speaker

        original_filename = self._resolve_original_filename(
            forum_post_info=merged,
            payload=payload,
            metadata=metadata,
            source_url="",
        )
        if original_filename:
            merged["original_filename"] = original_filename
        return merged

    def _normalize_text_list(self, *values: Any) -> List[str]:
        output: List[str] = []
        seen: set[str] = set()
        for value in values:
            items: List[str] = []
            if isinstance(value, list):
                items = [str(item or "").strip() for item in value]
            elif isinstance(value, str):
                items = [item.strip() for item in value.replace("\uFF0C", ",").split(",")]
            for item in items:
                normalized = " ".join(item.split())
                if not normalized:
                    continue
                dedup_key = normalized.lower()
                if dedup_key in seen:
                    continue
                seen.add(dedup_key)
                output.append(normalized)
        return output

    def _pick_first_text(self, *values: Any) -> str:
        for value in values:
            text = str(value or "").strip()
            if text:
                return text
        return ""

    def _sanitize_filename(self, value: str) -> str:
        text = str(value or "").strip()
        if not text:
            return ""
        text = text.replace("\\", "/").split("/")[-1].strip()
        text = re.sub(r"[\x00-\x1f]", "", text)
        text = re.sub(r"[<>:\"/\\\\|?*]+", "_", text)
        text = re.sub(r"\s+", " ", text).strip().strip(".")
        return text

    def _init_task_storage(self) -> Optional[SqliteStorageAdapter]:
        db_path = os.getenv("CLONECUT_DB_PATH", "data/clonecut.db")
        try:
            return SqliteStorageAdapter(db_path=db_path, logger=self.logger)
        except Exception as exc:
            self.logger.warning("sqlite storage disabled: %s", exc)
            return None

    def _save_task_snapshot(self, task: UnifiedTask) -> None:
        self._sync_task_metadata(task)
        if self.task_storage is None:
            return
        self.task_storage.save_task(task)

    def _persist_task(self, task: UnifiedTask) -> None:
        self._sync_task_metadata(task)
        self.registry.add(task)
        self._save_task_snapshot(task)

    def _sync_task_metadata(self, task: UnifiedTask) -> None:
        metadata = dict(task.metadata or {})
        metadata["current_stage"] = int(task.current_stage)
        metadata["max_retries"] = int(task.max_retries)
        metadata["retry_count"] = int(task.retry_count)
        if task.stage_checkpoint:
            metadata["stage_checkpoint"] = task.stage_checkpoint
        else:
            metadata.pop("stage_checkpoint", None)
        task.metadata = metadata

    def _transition_status(self, task: UnifiedTask, status: TaskStatus, strict: bool = True) -> bool:
        result = self.registry.update_status(task.task_id, status)
        if result.ok:
            task.status = status
            if status in {TaskStatus.PENDING, TaskStatus.FAILED, TaskStatus.CANCELLED}:
                task.started_at = None
            return True
        if strict:
            raise RuntimeError(result.reason or f"status transition failed: {task.task_id}")
        return False

    def _mark_task_active(self, task_id: str, active: bool) -> None:
        with self.lock:
            if active:
                self.active_task_ids.add(task_id)
            else:
                self.active_task_ids.discard(task_id)

    def _schedule_retry(self, task: UnifiedTask) -> bool:
        if task.status != TaskStatus.FAILED:
            return False
        retryable = bool((task.metadata or {}).get("retryable_failure", True))
        if not retryable:
            return False
        max_retries = max(0, int(task.max_retries))
        if task.retry_count >= max_retries:
            return False

        delay = self._retry_delay_seconds(task, task.retry_count)
        retry_count = task.retry_count + 1
        due_at = time.time() + delay
        task.retry_count = retry_count
        task.metadata = dict(task.metadata or {})
        task.metadata["retry_due_at"] = due_at
        task.metadata["retry_delay_seconds"] = delay
        self._persist_task(task)

        with self.lock:
            self.retry_index[task.task_id] = (due_at, task)
            heapq.heappush(self.retry_heap, (due_at, task.task_id))
            self.stats["retried"] += 1
        return True

    def _retry_delay_seconds(self, task: UnifiedTask, retry_count_before_increment: int) -> int:
        failed_from = str((task.metadata or {}).get("failed_from_status", "")).strip().lower()
        backoff = self.retry_backoff_seconds or [5]
        if failed_from == TaskStatus.UPLOADING.value:
            backoff = self.upload_retry_backoff_seconds or [1, 2, 4]
        idx = min(max(0, int(retry_count_before_increment)), len(backoff) - 1)
        return int(backoff[idx])

    def _is_retryable_failure(self, error: Exception, failed_from: TaskStatus) -> bool:
        if failed_from != TaskStatus.UPLOADING:
            return True
        if isinstance(error, RetryableUploadError):
            return True
        if isinstance(error, NonRetryableUploadError):
            return False
        return False

    def _remove_retry_schedule(self, task_id: str) -> None:
        with self.lock:
            self.retry_index.pop(task_id, None)

    def _retry_scheduler_loop(self) -> None:
        while not self.stop_event.is_set():
            ready = self._dequeue_ready_retries()
            for task in ready:
                self._enqueue_retry_task(task)
            self.stop_event.wait(self.retry_check_interval_seconds)

    def _dequeue_ready_retries(self) -> List[UnifiedTask]:
        now_ts = time.time()
        ready: List[UnifiedTask] = []
        with self.lock:
            while self.retry_heap:
                due_at, task_id = self.retry_heap[0]
                if due_at > now_ts:
                    break
                heapq.heappop(self.retry_heap)
                indexed = self.retry_index.get(task_id)
                if indexed is None:
                    continue
                idx_due_at, task = indexed
                if idx_due_at != due_at:
                    continue
                self.retry_index.pop(task_id, None)
                ready.append(task)
        return ready

    def _enqueue_retry_task(self, task: UnifiedTask) -> None:
        queue_name = self._queue_for_retry_task(task)
        task.metadata = dict(task.metadata or {})
        task.metadata.pop("retry_due_at", None)
        task.metadata.pop("retry_delay_seconds", None)
        task.metadata.pop("retryable_failure", None)
        task.error_message = None
        task.completed_at = None
        task.started_at = None
        transitioned = self._transition_status(task, TaskStatus.PENDING, strict=False)
        if not transitioned:
            task.status = TaskStatus.PENDING
            self._persist_task(task)
        else:
            self._persist_task(task)
        if queue_name == "upload":
            transitioned_upload = self._transition_status(task, TaskStatus.PROCESSING, strict=False)
            if not transitioned_upload:
                task.status = TaskStatus.PROCESSING
            self._persist_task(task)
        self._enqueue_task(queue_name, task)
        self.logger.info(
            "task retry enqueued: task_id=%s retry_count=%s/%s queue=%s",
            task.task_id,
            task.retry_count,
            task.max_retries,
            queue_name,
        )

    def _queue_for_retry_task(self, task: UnifiedTask) -> str:
        failed_from = str((task.metadata or {}).get("failed_from_status", "")).strip().lower()
        if failed_from == TaskStatus.UPLOADING.value and self._has_uploadable_output(task):
            return "upload"
        if failed_from == TaskStatus.DOWNLOADING.value and self._needs_download(task):
            return "download"
        if failed_from == TaskStatus.PROCESSING.value:
            return "process"
        return self._initial_queue_for_task(task)

    def _restore_retry_schedule(self) -> int:
        if not self.registry.is_persistent():
            return 0
        tasks = self.registry.list_by_status(TaskStatus.FAILED, limit=5000)
        restored = 0
        now_ts = time.time()
        for task in tasks:
            if int(task.retry_count) >= int(task.max_retries):
                continue
            retry_due_at_raw = (task.metadata or {}).get("retry_due_at")
            try:
                retry_due_at = float(retry_due_at_raw)
            except Exception:
                retry_due_at = now_ts
            with self.lock:
                self.retry_index[task.task_id] = (retry_due_at, task)
                heapq.heappush(self.retry_heap, (retry_due_at, task.task_id))
            restored += 1
        return restored

    def _zombie_cleaner_loop(self) -> None:
        while not self.stop_event.is_set():
            reclaimed = self._reclaim_zombies_once()
            if reclaimed > 0:
                with self.lock:
                    self.stats["zombie_reclaimed"] += reclaimed
            self.stop_event.wait(self.zombie_check_interval_seconds)

    def _reclaim_zombies_once(self) -> int:
        running_statuses = [
            TaskStatus.PENDING,
            TaskStatus.DOWNLOADING,
            TaskStatus.PROCESSING,
            TaskStatus.UPLOADING,
        ]
        reclaimed = 0
        for status in running_statuses:
            tasks = self.registry.list_by_status(status, limit=2000)
            for task in tasks:
                if status != TaskStatus.PENDING:
                    with self.lock:
                        if task.task_id in self.active_task_ids:
                            continue
                if not self._is_zombie_task(task, status):
                    continue
                age = int((datetime.now() - (task.started_at or task.created_at)).total_seconds())
                error = RuntimeError(
                    f"zombie task reclaimed after {age}s in status={status.value}"
                )
                self._fail_task(task, error, failed_from=status)
                reclaimed += 1
        return reclaimed

    def _is_zombie_task(self, task: UnifiedTask, status: TaskStatus) -> bool:
        timeout_seconds = float(
            self.zombie_timeout_by_status_seconds.get(status.value, self.zombie_timeout_seconds)
        )
        if timeout_seconds <= 0:
            return False
        if status == TaskStatus.PENDING:
            started_at = task.created_at
        else:
            started_at = task.started_at or task.assigned_at or task.created_at
        if started_at is None:
            return False
        age = (datetime.now() - started_at).total_seconds()
        return age > timeout_seconds

    def _build_zombie_timeout_by_status(self) -> Dict[str, float]:
        mapping_raw = self._get_worker_cfg("zombie_timeout_by_status_seconds", {})
        mapping = mapping_raw if isinstance(mapping_raw, dict) else {}
        defaults = {
            TaskStatus.PENDING.value: float(self.zombie_timeout_seconds),
            TaskStatus.DOWNLOADING.value: float(self.zombie_timeout_seconds),
            TaskStatus.PROCESSING.value: float(self.zombie_timeout_seconds),
            TaskStatus.UPLOADING.value: float(self.zombie_timeout_seconds),
        }
        resolved: Dict[str, float] = {}
        for status_value, default in defaults.items():
            per_status_key = f"zombie_timeout_{status_value}_seconds"
            per_status_value = self._get_worker_cfg(per_status_key, None)
            if per_status_value is not None:
                resolved[status_value] = self._coerce_timeout_seconds(per_status_value, default)
                continue
            map_value = mapping.get(status_value)
            if map_value is not None:
                resolved[status_value] = self._coerce_timeout_seconds(map_value, default)
                continue
            resolved[status_value] = float(default)
        return resolved

    def _coerce_timeout_seconds(self, value: Any, default: float) -> float:
        try:
            return max(5.0, float(value))
        except Exception:
            return max(5.0, float(default))

    def _recover_stuck_tasks(self) -> int:
        if not self.registry.is_persistent():
            return 0

        recoverable = [
            TaskStatus.ASSIGNED,
            TaskStatus.DOWNLOADING,
            TaskStatus.PROCESSING,
            TaskStatus.UPLOADING,
        ]
        recovered = 0
        for status in recoverable:
            tasks = self.registry.list_by_status(status, limit=2000)
            for task in tasks:
                queue_name = self._recovery_queue_for_task(task, status)
                next_status = TaskStatus.PROCESSING if queue_name == "upload" else TaskStatus.PENDING
                task.status = next_status
                if next_status == TaskStatus.PENDING:
                    task.started_at = None
                else:
                    task.started_at = task.started_at or datetime.now()
                task.completed_at = None
                self._persist_task(task)
                self._enqueue_task(queue_name, task)
                recovered += 1
        return recovered

    def _recovery_queue_for_task(self, task: UnifiedTask, old_status: TaskStatus) -> str:
        if old_status == TaskStatus.UPLOADING and self._has_uploadable_output(task):
            return "upload"
        if old_status == TaskStatus.PROCESSING:
            return "process"
        if old_status == TaskStatus.FAILED:
            return self._queue_for_retry_task(task)
        if old_status == TaskStatus.DOWNLOADING and self._needs_download(task):
            return "download"
        return self._initial_queue_for_task(task)

    def _get_queue_cfg(self, key: str, default: Any) -> Any:
        raw_queue = {}
        if isinstance(getattr(self.config, "raw", None), dict):
            raw_queue = self.config.raw.get("queue", {}) or {}
        env_key = f"CLONECUT_QUEUE_{key}".upper()
        env_val = os.getenv(env_key)
        if env_val is not None:
            return self._cast_cfg_value(env_val, default)
        if key in raw_queue:
            return self._cast_cfg_value(raw_queue.get(key), default)
        return default

    def _parse_retry_backoff(self, raw: Any) -> List[int]:
        if isinstance(raw, list):
            values = raw
        elif isinstance(raw, str):
            text = raw.strip()
            values = [item.strip() for item in text.split(",") if item.strip()]
        else:
            values = [5, 10, 20]

        parsed: List[int] = []
        for item in values:
            try:
                parsed.append(max(1, int(item)))
            except Exception:
                continue
        if not parsed:
            parsed = [5, 10, 20]
        return parsed

    def _get_worker_cfg(self, key: str, default: Any) -> Any:
        raw_worker = {}
        if isinstance(getattr(self.config, "raw", None), dict):
            raw_worker = self.config.raw.get("worker", {}) or {}

        env_key = f"CLONECUT_WORKER_{key}".upper()
        env_val = os.getenv(env_key)
        if env_val is not None:
            return self._cast_cfg_value(env_val, default)
        if key in raw_worker:
            return self._cast_cfg_value(raw_worker.get(key), default)
        return default

    def _cast_cfg_value(self, value: Any, default: Any) -> Any:
        if isinstance(default, bool):
            if isinstance(value, bool):
                return value
            return str(value).strip().lower() == "true"
        if isinstance(default, int):
            try:
                return int(value)
            except Exception:
                return default
        if isinstance(default, float):
            try:
                return float(value)
            except Exception:
                return default
        return value

    def _bool_cfg(self, raw: Optional[str], default: bool) -> bool:
        if raw is None:
            return default
        return raw.strip().lower() == "true"

    def _extract_optional_bool(self, *values: Any) -> Optional[bool]:
        for value in values:
            if value is None:
                continue
            if isinstance(value, bool):
                return value
            text = str(value).strip().lower()
            if not text:
                continue
            if text in {"1", "true", "yes", "y", "on"}:
                return True
            if text in {"0", "false", "no", "n", "off"}:
                return False
        return None

    def _queryable_statuses(self) -> List[TaskStatus]:
        return [
            TaskStatus.PENDING,
            TaskStatus.ASSIGNED,
            TaskStatus.DOWNLOADING,
            TaskStatus.PROCESSING,
            TaskStatus.UPLOADING,
            TaskStatus.COMPLETED,
            TaskStatus.FAILED,
            TaskStatus.CANCELLED,
        ]

    def _resolve_status_filter(self, status: Optional[str]) -> List[TaskStatus]:
        if status is None:
            return self._queryable_statuses()
        raw = str(status).strip().lower()
        if not raw or raw == "all":
            return self._queryable_statuses()
        known = {item.value for item in self._queryable_statuses()}
        if raw not in known:
            raise ValueError(f"invalid status filter: {status}")
        return [parse_task_status(raw)]

from __future__ import annotations

import json
import os
from pathlib import Path
from typing import Any
from typing import Optional

from .base import StageResult
from .utils import ensure_stage_dir, stage_artifact_path


def run_stage5_ai_text(
    input_video: str,
    output_dir: str,
    task_id: str,
    *,
    forum_post_info: Optional[dict] = None,
) -> StageResult:
    source = Path(input_video)
    stage_dir = ensure_stage_dir(output_dir, task_id)
    task_root = Path(output_dir) / task_id
    if not source.exists():
        return StageResult(success=False, output_file=input_video, error_message="stage5 input missing")

    script_path = stage_artifact_path(output_dir, task_id, "stage5_ai_script", ".txt")
    pointer_path = stage_artifact_path(output_dir, task_id, "stage5_script_path", ".txt")
    manifest_path = stage_artifact_path(output_dir, task_id, "stage5_ai_manifest", ".json")
    clip_text_path = task_root / "clip_text.txt"
    script_text = "Script Draft\n\nKey Points:\n- skeleton output\n"
    script_path.write_text(script_text, encoding="utf-8")
    clip_text_path.write_text(script_text, encoding="utf-8")
    pointer_path.write_text(str(script_path), encoding="utf-8")
    use_forum_keywords = os.getenv("CLONECUT_STAGE5_USE_FORUM_KEYWORDS", "true").strip().lower() == "true"
    hotwords = []
    raw_hotwords = forum_post_info.get("hotwords", []) if isinstance(forum_post_info, dict) else []
    if use_forum_keywords:
        seen: set[str] = set()
        for item in raw_hotwords:
            text = str(item).strip()
            if not text or text in seen:
                continue
            seen.add(text)
            hotwords.append(text)
    llm_use_factory = os.getenv("CLONECUT_STAGE5_LLM_USE_FACTORY", "false").strip().lower() == "true"
    llm_provider = os.getenv("CLONECUT_STAGE5_LLM_PROVIDER", "rule").strip().lower()
    strict = os.getenv("CLONECUT_STRICT_EQUIVALENCE", "false").strip().lower() == "true"
    engine = "rule_based"
    llm_error = ""
    fallback_used = False
    strict_rejected = False
    if llm_use_factory and llm_provider == "rule":
        engine = "llm_factory:rule"
    elif llm_use_factory and llm_provider != "rule":
        engine = "rule_based"
        llm_error = "missing api_key for provider"
        fallback_used = True
        if strict:
            strict_rejected = True

    manifest_path.write_text(
        json.dumps(
            {
                "task_id": task_id,
                "forum_post_info": forum_post_info or {},
                "engine": engine,
                "keywords": hotwords,
                "use_forum_keywords": use_forum_keywords,
                "forum_keyword_count": len(hotwords),
                "llm_use_factory": llm_use_factory,
                "llm_error": llm_error,
                "fallback_used": fallback_used,
                "strict_rejected": strict_rejected,
            },
            ensure_ascii=False,
            indent=2,
        ),
        encoding="utf-8",
    )
    if strict_rejected:
        return StageResult(
            success=False,
            output_file=str(source),
            error_message="strict equivalence rejected stage5 fallback",
            artifacts={"manifest_file": str(manifest_path)},
        )
    return StageResult(success=True, output_file=str(source), artifacts={"manifest_file": str(manifest_path)})


def run(*args: Any, **kwargs: Any) -> StageResult:
    return run_stage5_ai_text(*args, **kwargs)

def _build_config(tmp_path) -> SimpleNamespace:  # type: ignore[no-untyped-def]
    ns_hash = hashlib.md5(str(tmp_path).encode("utf-8")).hexdigest()
    namespace = f"clonecut_worker_unit_{ns_hash}:"
    return SimpleNamespace(
        redis_host="127.0.0.1",
        redis_port=6379,
        redis_db=0,
        redis_password="",
        redis_namespace=namespace,
        input_dir=str(tmp_path / "input"),
        output_dir=str(tmp_path / "output"),
        log_dir=str(tmp_path / "logs"),
        raw={
            "queue": {
                "max_retries": 2,
                "retry_backoff_seconds": [1, 1, 1],
            },
            "worker": {
                "max_download_workers": 1,
                "max_process_workers": 1,
                "max_upload_workers": 1,

                "zombie_timeout_seconds": 1,

def test_video_task_flows_download_process_upload(monkeypatch, tmp_path) -> None:  # type: ignore[no-untyped-def]
    monkeypatch.setenv("CLONECUT_DB_PATH", str(tmp_path / "clonecut.db"))
    cfg = _build_config(tmp_path)
    service = WorkerService(cfg)

    source = tmp_path / "source.mp4"
    source.write_bytes(b"video-content")

    service.start()
    try:
        ok, task_id, error = service.submit(
            {
                "task_type": "video",
                "source_url": str(source),
                "metadata": {"source": "unit"},
            }
        )
        assert ok
        assert not error
        assert task_id

        deadline = time.time() + 10
        final_task = None
        while time.time() < deadline:
            final_task = service.get_task(task_id)
            if final_task and final_task.get("status") == "completed":
                break
            time.sleep(0.05)

        assert isinstance(final_task, dict)
        assert final_task.get("status") == "completed"
        assert Path(str(final_task.get("source_path"))).exists()

        result = final_task.get("result")
        assert isinstance(result, dict)
        assert result.get("engine") == "internal_pipeline_auto"
        upload = result.get("upload")
        assert isinstance(upload, dict)
        uploaded_path = upload.get("uploaded_path")
        assert isinstance(uploaded_path, str) and uploaded_path
        assert Path(uploaded_path).exists()
    finally:
        service.stop()


def test_failed_task_auto_retries_until_success(monkeypatch, tmp_path) -> None:  # type: ignore[no-untyped-def]
    monkeypatch.setenv("CLONECUT_DB_PATH", str(tmp_path / "clonecut_retry.db"))
    cfg = _build_config(tmp_path)
    service = WorkerService(cfg)
    source = tmp_path / "retry-source.mp4"
    source.write_bytes(b"video-content")

    original = service._process_video_like
    attempts = {"count": 0}

    def flaky_process(task):  # type: ignore[no-untyped-def]
        attempts["count"] += 1
        if attempts["count"] == 1:
            raise RuntimeError("inject process failure")
        return original(task)

    service._process_video_like = flaky_process  # type: ignore[method-assign]

    service.start()
    try:
        ok, task_id, error = service.submit(
            {
                "task_type": "video",
                "source_url": str(source),
                "metadata": {"source": "retry-test"},
            }
        )
        assert ok
        assert not error

        deadline = time.time() + 15
        final_task = None
        while time.time() < deadline:
            final_task = service.get_task(task_id)
            if final_task and final_task.get("status") == "completed" and attempts["count"] >= 2:
                break
            time.sleep(0.1)

        assert attempts["count"] >= 2
        assert isinstance(final_task, dict)
        assert final_task.get("status") == "completed"
        assert int(final_task.get("retry_count", 0)) >= 1
    finally:
        service.stop()

def test_zombie_task_reclaimed_then_requeued(monkeypatch, tmp_path) -> None:  # type: ignore[no-untyped-def]
    monkeypatch.setenv("CLONECUT_DB_PATH", str(tmp_path / "clonecut_zombie.db"))
    cfg = _build_config(tmp_path)
    service = WorkerService(cfg)

    zombie = UnifiedTask(
        task_id="zombie-1",
        task_type=TaskType.VIDEO,
        source="unit",
        source_url=str(tmp_path / "missing.mp4"),
        status=TaskStatus.PROCESSING,
        current_stage=3,
        stage_checkpoint="stage3_repair",
        max_retries=1,
    )
    zombie.started_at = datetime.now() - timedelta(seconds=40)
    service._persist_task(zombie)

    reclaimed = service._reclaim_zombies_once()
    assert reclaimed == 1

    time.sleep(1.2)
    ready = service._dequeue_ready_retries()
    assert len(ready) == 1
    service._enqueue_retry_task(ready[0])

    queued = service.queue_adapter.pop_process(timeout=0.1)
    assert queued is not None
    assert queued.task_id == "zombie-1"
    loaded = service.get_task("zombie-1")
    assert isinstance(loaded, dict)
    assert loaded.get("status") == "pending"


def test_zombie_reclaim_uses_status_specific_thresholds(monkeypatch, tmp_path) -> None:  # type: ignore[no-untyped-def]
    monkeypatch.setenv("CLONECUT_DB_PATH", str(tmp_path / "clonecut_zombie_threshold.db"))
    cfg = _build_config(tmp_path)
    cfg.raw["worker"]["zombie_timeout_by_status_seconds"] = {
        "pending": 1,
        "downloading": 120,
        "processing": 120,
        "uploading": 120,
    }
    service = WorkerService(cfg)

    pending_task = UnifiedTask(
        task_id="pending-zombie-1",
        task_type=TaskType.VIDEO,
        source="unit",
        source_url=str(tmp_path / "pending.mp4"),
        status=TaskStatus.PENDING,
    )
    pending_task.created_at = datetime.now() - timedelta(seconds=10)
    service._persist_task(pending_task)

    processing_task = UnifiedTask(
        task_id="processing-fresh-1",
        task_type=TaskType.VIDEO,
        source="unit",
        source_url=str(tmp_path / "processing.mp4"),
        status=TaskStatus.PROCESSING,
    )
    processing_task.started_at = datetime.now() - timedelta(seconds=10)
    service._persist_task(processing_task)

    reclaimed = service._reclaim_zombies_once()
    assert reclaimed == 1

    pending_loaded = service.get_task("pending-zombie-1")
    processing_loaded = service.get_task("processing-fresh-1")
    assert isinstance(pending_loaded, dict)
    assert isinstance(processing_loaded, dict)
